    She's referring to profound human experiences and virtues like love, kindness, compassion, joy, and inner peace. These are the things that give life its greatest meaning and richness.     The quote also speaks to appreciating the immaterial essence of things, not just their external appearance. A breathtaking sunset is beautiful to look at, but even more moving is the awe, wonder and emotional connection we feel when experiencing it.

    Additionally, Keller, who was blind and deaf from a young age, is reminding us that perceiving the world isn't limited to sight and the other senses. The heart and spirit have a perception all their own, one that runs deeper than the physical.

    Ultimately, this quote is an invitation to connect with what matters most - the love, beauty, meaning and sacred experiences we carry in our hearts. That is where we discover life's greatest joys and most profound truths. The external is temporary, but what we feel inside endures.

    1. Decide what kind of chicken you want - there are many breeds available for different purposes like egg laying, meat production, or as pets. Some common breeds include Rhode Island Reds, Orpingtons, and Silkies.

    2. Find a reputable breeder, hatchery or farm supply store in your area that sells chickens. You can search online or ask for recommendations from other chicken owners.

    3. Contact the seller to see what breeds they have available and at what age/size. Day-old chicks, started pullets (young hens), and adult birds may be options.

    4. Ask about the health of their flock and what vaccinations the birds have had. Healthy stock from a clean environment is important.

    5. Determine if you want to buy sexed female chicks (pullets), males (cockerels) or a "straight run" of mixed sex. Males crow and don't lay eggs.

    6. Prepare proper housing, feed, water and safety for your new chicken in advance. They will need a draft-free coop with roosting bars, nesting boxes, and an enclosed run.

    7. Bring the chicken home in a ventilated box or carrier. Handle it gently as it adjusts to its new surroundings.

    8. Provide your chicken daily care, quality feed, clean water, and secure shelter. Regular health checks and vet care if needed will help it thrive.

    Let me know if you have any other questions! Raising backyard chickens can be a fun and rewarding experience.
